# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes apimachinery runtime.Object Import Chain

## Your Task

Trace how k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object is imported and used across kubernetes/kubernetes. Find all Go source files in the core/v1 API types that implement runtime.Object by embedding TypeMeta and ObjectMeta, and the files in the API machinery that register these types into the scheme.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [

  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced the `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object` import chain across the Kubernetes codebase. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**Core Runtime Interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime/interfaces.go`):
- Defines the `Object` interface that all API types must implement
- Requires two methods: `GetObjectKind()` and `DeepCopyObject()`

**Type Definitions**:
1. **`runtime.TypeMeta`** - in `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime/types.go` (lines 38-43)
2. **`metav1.TypeMeta`** - redefined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/types.go` (lines 42-57)
3. **`metav1.ObjectMeta`** - defined in the same file (lines 109+) with all standard Kubernetes metadata

**Core/v1 Types** (`staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/types.go`):
- All core API types implement `runtime.Object` by embedding both `metav1.TypeMeta` and `metav1.ObjectMeta`
- Examples: Pod, Service, Node, Namespace, Secret, ConfigMap, Event, ReplicationController, etc.

**Registration Mechanism**:
- `addKnownTypes()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/register.go` registers all core/v1 types
- `AddToGroupVersion()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/register.go` registers metav1 types
- These flow through `Scheme.AddKnownTypes()` for serialization/deserialization

The complete answer with all files, symbols, and detailed explanation has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

The proper way to use it is to inline it in your type,\\n23: // like this:\\n24: //\\n25: //\\ttype MyAwesomeAPIObject struct {\\n26: //\\t     runtime.TypeMeta    `json:\\\",inline\\\"`\\n27: //\\t     ... // other fields\\n28: //\\t}\\n29: //\\n30: // func (obj *MyAwesomeAPIObject) SetGroupVersionKind(gvk *metav1.GroupVersionKind) { metav1.UpdateTypeMeta(obj,gvk) }; GroupVersionKind() *GroupVersionKind\\n31: //\\n32: // TypeMeta is provided here for convenience. You may use it directly from this package or define\\n33: // your own with the same fields.\\n34: //\\n35: // +k8s:deepcopy-gen=false\\n36: // +protobuf=true\\n37: // +k8s:openapi-gen=true\\n38: type TypeMeta struct {\\n39: \\t// +optional\\n40: \\tAPIVersion string `json:\\\"apiVersion,omitempty\\\" yaml:\\\"apiVersion,omitempty\\\" protobuf:\\\"bytes,1,opt,name=apiVersion\\\"`\\n41: \\t// +optional\\n42: \\tKind string `json:\\\"kind,omitempty\\\" yaml:\\\"kind,omitempty\\\" protobuf:\\\"bytes,2,opt,name=kind\\\"`\\n43: }\\n44: \\n45: const (\\n46: \\tContentTypeJSON         string = \\\"application/json\\\"\\n47: \\tContentTypeYAML         string = \\\"application/yaml\\\"\\n48: \\tContentTypeProtobuf     string = \\\"application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf\\\"\\n49: \\tContentTypeCBOR         string = \\\"application/cbor\\\"     // RFC 8949\\n50: \\tContentTypeCBORSequence string = \\\"application/cbor-seq\\\" // RFC 8742\\n51: )\\n52: \\n53: // RawExtension is used to hold extensions in external versions.\\n54: //\\n55: // To use this, make a field which has RawExtension as its type in your external, versioned\\n56: // struct, and Object in your internal struct. You also need to register your\\n57: // various plugin types.\\n58: //\\n59: // // Internal package:\\n60: //\\n61: //\\ttype MyAPIObject struct {\\n62: //\\t\\truntime.TypeMeta `json:\\\",inline\\\"`\\n63: //\\t\\tMyPlugin runtime.Object `json:\\\"myPlugin\\\"`\\n64: //\\t}\\n65: //\\n66: //\\ttype PluginA struct {\\n67: //\\t\\tAOption string `json:\\\"aOption\\\"`\\n68: //\\t}\\n69: //\\n70: // // External package:\\n71: //\\n72: //\\ttype MyAPIObject struct {\\n73: //\\t\\truntime.TypeMeta `json:\\\",inline\\\"`\\n74: //\\t\\tMyPlugin runtime.RawExtension `json:\\\"myPlugin\\\"`\\n75: //\\t}\\n76: //\\n77: //\\ttype PluginA struct {\\n78: //\\t\\tAOption string `json:\\\"aOption\\\"`\\n79: //\\t}\\n80: //\\n81: // // On the wire, the JSON will look something like this:\\n82: //\\n83: //\\t{\\n84: //\\t\\t\\\"kind\\\":\\\"MyAPIObject\\\",\\n85: //\\t\\t\\\"apiVersion\\\":\\\"v1\\\",\\n86: //\\t\\t\\\"myPlugin\\\": {\\n87: //\\t\\t\\t\\\"kind\\\":\\\"PluginA\\\",\\n88: //\\t\\t\\t\\\"aOption\\\":\\\"foo\\\",\\n89: //\\t\\t},\\n90: //\\t}\\n91: //\\n92: // So what happens? Decode first uses json or yaml to unmarshal the serialized data into\\n93: // your external MyAPIObject. That causes the raw JSON to be stored, but not unpacked.\\n94: // The next step is to copy (using pkg/conversion) into the internal struct. The runtime\\n95: // package's DefaultScheme has conversion functions installed which will unpack the\\n96: // JSON stored in RawExtension, turning it into the correct object type, and storing it\\n97: // in the Object.
